With the economy in a decent position, many believed that Dorgan had a fighting chance. Still, the Farmer-Labor Party was divided, and it seemed that Keyes' stance on social issues would win the day. After a tough campaign, Dorgan scraped by with 48.4% of the vote to Keyes' 48.1%. A national recount was conducted over the course of November, but decent enough returns in California and New York gave Dorgan the votes needed to be elected President of the United States. It remains the closest race since the Nonpartisan League brought together the political left to form the current party system in 1952.

1932 United States presidential election

From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia

The 1932 United States presidential election was the 37th quadrennial presidential election, held on Tuesday, November 8, 1932. The election took place against the backdrop of the Great Depression. The incumbent Republican President Calvin Coolidge was defeated in a landslide by Progressive Upton Sinclair, with Democrat James Reed taking second place. Sinclair was the first third-party candidate to win a Presidential election, and the first non-Democratic or non-Republican President since Millard Fillmore in the 1850s.

The election marked the effective end of the Fourth Party System, which had been dominated by Republicans. Despite disastrous economic conditions due to the Great Depression, Coolidge easily defeated opposition such as Herbert Hoover at the 1932 Republican National Convention. Reed was widely considered the front-runner after the 1932 Democratic National Convention, but began to lose ground to the third-party Progressive ticket during the fall campaign. The collapse of the Republican campaign largely benefitted Sinclair's bid, although Reed gained conservative voters as well.

Sinclair won both a majority in the electoral and a plurality of the popular votes, carrying the west and winning nearly every industrial midwest and northern state.

While he only served for eight years, frequent rankings of Supreme Court justices often place him in the upper tier of Justices, possibly being ranked the best. While his judicial experience is undoubtable, there is one clear mistake that he made.
